  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_7f7a705c-04cb-4497-8766-e5b500e2d0ed'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText7421734977940074955" style="display:none">When a minority race of telepaths is suspected of causing a near-devastating tidal wave, Private Kaylin Neya is summoned to Court—and into a PR nightmare. To ease racial tensions, the emperor has commissioned a play, and the playwright has his own ideas about who should be the focus.…<br /><br />But Kaylin works her best magic behind the scenes, and though she tries to stay neutral, she is again drawn into a world of politics—and murder. To make matters worse, Marcus, her trusted sergeant, gets stripped of his command, leaving Kaylin vulnerable. Now she's juggling two troubling cases, and even magic's looking good by comparison. But then nobody ever said life in the theater was easy.…</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1674380742?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justine" href="/user/show/18656418-justine">Justine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18656418-justine?shelf=2017-read">2017-read</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1674380742" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8275142538737154340">Another solid entry in the Chronicles of Elantra. As usual, the story picks up shortly after the events of the previous book. The racial prejudice that Kaylin successfully confronted herself still prevails in Elantra in the aftermath of events that nearly destroyed the city. <br/><br/>In the midst of this, a new challenge arises for Kaylin and Severn when their Sargeant, Marcus, is held for murder of a fellow Leontine. As this is being dealt with by the Caste Courts, Kaylin and Servern have no jurisdictio</span>
  <span id="freeText8275142538737154340" style="display:none">Another solid entry in the Chronicles of Elantra. As usual, the story picks up shortly after the events of the previous book. The racial prejudice that Kaylin successfully confronted herself still prevails in Elantra in the aftermath of events that nearly destroyed the city. <br /><br />In the midst of this, a new challenge arises for Kaylin and Severn when their Sargeant, Marcus, is held for murder of a fellow Leontine. As this is being dealt with by the Caste Courts, Kaylin and Servern have no jurisdiction to act or investigate, but of course that doesn't stop them from trying to exonerate Marcus.<br /><br />I loved the more in-depth look that this book gave at the Leontine race. Every book has opened a new door into the world of Elantra, and the results are always richly satisfying. Sagara has really found her feet in this world, and I still find her descriptions of events where magic is used to be among the most evocative I've read. She is an emotive writer, and does a great job of making the reader feel invested in the various characters.<br /><br />On to the next book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6304351.Cast_in_Silence__Chronicles_of_Elantra___5_" title="Cast in Silence (Chronicles of Elantra, #5) by Michelle Sagara" rel="nofollow noopener">Cast in Silence</a>!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8275142538737154340" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22911953-monty-cupcake-queen-of-bloodshed?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22911953-monty-cupcake-queen-of-bloodshed?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2178820815" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18000987538854518648">I think I liked this one less than the last one. It doesn't have a lot of Nightshade in it - who knew I'd miss that guy, but I did. He's a nice and mysterious one. There's more dragons and Severn still, yay. This time around it's all about the Lions and a playwright. <br/><br/>Kaylin & Severn are the cultural consultants to Rennick, the Imperial playwright, writing a play on the Tha'lanni (tentacle mind readers). This part was super boring and I didn't enjoy it. <br/><br/>As usual, there's something that Kaylin had</span>
  <span id="freeText18000987538854518648" style="display:none">I think I liked this one less than the last one. It doesn't have a lot of Nightshade in it - who knew I'd miss that guy, but I did. He's a nice and mysterious one. There's more dragons and Severn still, yay. This time around it's all about the Lions and a playwright. <br /><br />Kaylin &amp; Severn are the cultural consultants to Rennick, the Imperial playwright, writing a play on the Tha'lanni (tentacle mind readers). This part was super boring and I didn't enjoy it. <br /><br />As usual, there's something that Kaylin had to get involved in. Marcus, her lion boss, has been accused to murder, arrested, and on trial. She takes it upon herself to investigate and prove his innocence. I liked the lion people, interesting and definitely gave them a lot of back story. Made them more complicated than just lion people. <br /><br />Much better end battle. I think my real complaint is the side plot of the playwright and the continuation of Kaylin having no idea what she's doing. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer987984992" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12243954784837073871">*** 4.55 ***<br/><br/>This was,... it was... gosh, heartbreakingly beautiful and emotionally devastating, wonderful story! I realize that not everyone will feel the same, and I am cool with that, since I am well aware that I am a tenderhearted sap... And maybe almost 5 stars might be a tad too high a rating, but I finally figured out why I am so drawn to this series. Yes it has a fun fantastic world, yes the main protagonist is a cool girl who kicks ass, and most of all, there are DRAGONS!!! But what has </span>
  <span id="freeText12243954784837073871" style="display:none">*** 4.55 ***<br /><br />This was,... it was... gosh, heartbreakingly beautiful and emotionally devastating, wonderful story! I realize that not everyone will feel the same, and I am cool with that, since I am well aware that I am a tenderhearted sap... And maybe almost 5 stars might be a tad too high a rating, but I finally figured out why I am so drawn to this series. Yes it has a fun fantastic world, yes the main protagonist is a cool girl who kicks ass, and most of all, there are DRAGONS!!! But what has sunk its hooks into my heart is the way the author keeps creating new and developing old "mother" characters!!! And not the superficial, milky, or just there kind of mothers. These are the tough, claw sharpening, growling, hugging, overprotective, forgiving, helping you through your mistakes, encouraging, and for ever and always loving mothers who would defend your choices and pray for your wellbeing with their last breath!!! I know, I know, as I warned earlier, I am an emotional sap!!! I think the last 15% of the book I tried to read through tears and that is not easy at all!!! <br /><br />So, if you feel like falling in love with characters of worth and are prepared for some mushier feels, this book is for you. O, and did I mention DRAGONS!?!?!?</span>
  <a data-text-id="12243954784837073871" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17648854162090209588">It's time to take a closer look at the Leontines *happy* Markus is one of my favourite characters of the series and the Leontines seem to have a peculiar social structure similar enough to a pride but with some major differences. Markus' Pridlea are great, fierce females and I love the way they intereact with each other and with Kaylin.The origin story of this race was fascinating and only opened a door to more questions regarding these Ancient Ones. <br/><br/>Getting to know more about the races inhabiti</span>
  <span id="freeText17648854162090209588" style="display:none">It's time to take a closer look at the Leontines *happy* Markus is one of my favourite characters of the series and the Leontines seem to have a peculiar social structure similar enough to a pride but with some major differences. Markus' Pridlea are great, fierce females and I love the way they intereact with each other and with Kaylin.The origin story of this race was fascinating and only opened a door to more questions regarding these Ancient Ones. <br /><br />Getting to know more about the races inhabiting Elantra is my favorite part of the books which came as a surprise because I usually dislike extensive worldbuilding. But since there almost no character development (Kaylin is still the ignorant fool she was at the beginning of the series) I guess my attention got snatched by something else. I'm liking Lord Sanabalis more and more with each instalment. <br /><br />The third major plotline - helping the Imperial Playwright to prepare a new play that makes the Thaalani look more human was a bit boring. Yet from elantran's POV it was probably the most important as they are the most misunderstood race in the Empire. And they deserve to be left to live in peace. <br /><br />I hope that the next book will deal with the Aeriens since just like Kaylin I find them fascinating and would most likely spend a lot of time pestering them to fly me for a while. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15266712158517094180">Kaylin is a Hawk. An investigative cop in a realm where safety is relative. Where each case is defined by the neighborhood and the magical species involved. And just how many superiors Kaylin will manage to offend.<br/><br/>When Marcus, i.e. her boss—who also happens to be a Leontine (super large catlike person with a serious antipathy for paperwork) is accused of murder, there really isn’t any question of whether Kaylin will get involved.<br/><br/>Only of how many rules she will have to break.<br/><br/>Cast in Fury is the f</span>
  <span id="freeText15266712158517094180" style="display:none">Kaylin is a Hawk. An investigative cop in a realm where safety is relative. Where each case is defined by the neighborhood and the magical species involved. And just how many superiors Kaylin will manage to offend.<br /><br />When Marcus, i.e. her boss—who also happens to be a Leontine (super large catlike person with a serious antipathy for paperwork) is accused of murder, there really isn’t any question of whether Kaylin will get involved.<br /><br />Only of how many rules she will have to break.<br /><br />Cast in Fury is the fourth book in the Chronicles of Elantra. High-fantasy, which always feels a bit over my head, but I love Kaylin and her partner, Severn, (both humans) and the unveiling of their past, as well as Kaylin’s serious devotion to protecting the children of every species within Elantra.<br /><br />Of course, this book’s particular focus on giant catlike animals doesn’t hurt! <br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4401737133974771924">*Fantasy* Dragons, Magic, Fantasy<br/>*Rating* 3.5-4.0<br/><br/>First Thoughts!<br/><br/>I really like this series! Seriously I do.   <span id="freeText4401737133974771924" style="display:none">*Fantasy* Dragons, Magic, Fantasy<br />*Rating* 3.5-4.0<br /><br />First Thoughts!<br /><br />I really like this series! Seriously I do. I love the world building. I love the turmoil that Kaylin gets into time and time again. I love the fact that she somehow, someway manages to thwart the bad guys designs with her Old One's magic that hasn't been fully explored as of yet. You learn something new about Kaylin's abilities every time out and not even those around her can imagine what she is capable of.<br /><br />I also love Merrin. I love the fact that she takes in lost and troubled kids and molds them into amazing people. I still want to learn where the tattoos that are on Kaylin's body came from. They are steeped in mystery, yet, contain all sorts of magical mysteries. I also love the different kinds of characters that this series has to offer. Everything from Dragons to Lions, and a few other races like Aerians and Barrani. I still want to know about Kaylin and Lord Nightshade and what it means to be Erenne. I also know that there are plenty more books for me to read to have that explanation explained to me in greater detail! <br /><br /></span>

  <span id="freeText15935192551147301153" style="display:none">3.5 stars.<br /><br />Re-listened Jan 2020. As the author noted, this book goes into the culture norms of the Leontine race. <br /><br />When Marcus, Kaylin's Leontine Sergeant, is arrested for murder, Kaylin has the Hawk Lord's unofficial sanction to "stick her nose" into the case. What she discovered are some very long-held prejudices that Leontine babies born with certain physical characteristics have to be put to death. And that it involves the Leontine baby she helped delivered in the previous book. We've come to know how Kaylin feels about kids so naturally she's willing to fight the whole Leontine race as well as the Dragon Emperor to save both the baby and his mother. <br /><br />I'm not sure about the ending though <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ especially with the mother being killed off and leaving Kaylin with the baby.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <div id="review_1029383122" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1029383122" />
    <a title="J.A. Ironside" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15975161-j-a-ironside"><img alt="J.A. Ironside" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1454955023p2/15975161.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1029383122?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J.A. Ironside" class="user" itemprop="url" name="J.A. Ironside" href="/user/show/15975161-j-a-ironside">J.A. Ironside</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15975161-j-a-ironside?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15975161-j-a-ironside?shelf=audio-books">audio-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1029383122" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3742206540570903830">Ok this is a vast improvement on the previous couple if books. Really liked this one. As usual it's a fantasy police procedural which engages with themes of family vs found family, cultural clashes, law vs justice, and the marginalisation of individuals. The prose has tightened up a lot. Far less repetition and clunky dialogue. There was even a little humour which I found refreshing. The story follows Kaylin who is assigned to ensure that the royal playwrite produces a play that eases public opi</span>
  <span id="freeText3742206540570903830" style="display:none">Ok this is a vast improvement on the previous couple if books. Really liked this one. As usual it's a fantasy police procedural which engages with themes of family vs found family, cultural clashes, law vs justice, and the marginalisation of individuals. The prose has tightened up a lot. Far less repetition and clunky dialogue. There was even a little humour which I found refreshing. The story follows Kaylin who is assigned to ensure that the royal playwrite produces a play that eases public opinion to the telepathic Tha'elani without insulted an entire race of people. Midway through this less than choice assignment, Kaylin's boss is arrested for the murder of another Leontine (cat person) and a new acting chief is appointed - who Kaylin dispises. Marcus might be facing a death sentence but Kaylin is sure he's innocent. The problem is that Marcus refuses to talk. Kaylin is forced to unravel the complucated history of the Leontines and find out why Marcus will not defend himself. <br /><br />It's a clever exploration of what happens when cultural custom comes up against general law. The stakes were high and there's plenty of action. This time the phenominal world building encased a gripping story and Kaylin has grown as a character. Really enjoyed this one and will continue with the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3742206540570903830" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2179547309" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2179547309" />
    <a title="Emilee Powell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23562059-emilee-powell"><img alt="Emilee Powell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1378001079p2/23562059.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2179547309?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emilee Powell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emilee Powell" href="/user/show/23562059-emilee-powell">Emilee Powell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2179547309" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12338922622492707153">This author is in desperate need of a better editor. Not only were there a few traditional editing problems, the author needs to be reminded that after the fiftieth time of mentioning in the series that orange dragon eyes means danger and red dragon eyes means duck and cover, you really only have to mention that fact once or twice in the next books in the series. Or assume that your readers aren't complete idiots and let them figure it out in the continuing books using situational clues. Also, w</span>
  <span id="freeText12338922622492707153" style="display:none">This author is in desperate need of a better editor. Not only were there a few traditional editing problems, the author needs to be reminded that after the fiftieth time of mentioning in the series that orange dragon eyes means danger and red dragon eyes means duck and cover, you really only have to mention that fact once or twice in the next books in the series. Or assume that your readers aren't complete idiots and let them figure it out in the continuing books using situational clues. Also, while I have accepted it as a aggravating trait of the author that every time she describes a dragon's tone as being dry it is inevitably some variation of "so dry a spark could set it on fire," it is such an entirely overused phrase her editor should have marked her use of the phrase in regards to other characters with a red pen big old nope. While I am fond of this series characters and find the world interesting, the plot is repetitive and the writing is not the best. Frankly, I'm not entirely sure why I enjoy this series so much, but I do. However, Gina I sincerely hope that you do not read this series, you would have to rewrite it entirely in order to enjoy it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12338922622492707153" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_169710871" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/169710871" />
    <a title="Liz (Quirky Cat)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5473188-liz-quirky-cat"><img alt="Liz (Quirky Cat)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562812375p2/5473188.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/169710871?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz (Quirky Cat)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz (Quirky Cat)" href="/user/show/5473188-liz-quirky-cat">Liz (Quirky Cat)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5473188-liz-quirky-cat?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5473188-liz-quirky-cat?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5473188-liz-quirky-cat?shelf=mage">mage</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer169710871" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9022131943457446399">From the moment I first got my hands on a Chronicles of Elantra novel, I was hooked. Now, the series is fifteen books in (with the sixteenth on the way), and about to release a prequel novel focused on one of my favorite characters (Severn). To say I am extremely excited would be an understatement.<br/><br/>	As such, obviously I had to join the blog tour celebrating this new release. Part of that tour involves re-reading the series (yes!), and reviewing the novels we love so much. <br/><br/>	Cast in Fury is the fou</span>
  <span id="freeText9022131943457446399" style="display:none">From the moment I first got my hands on a Chronicles of Elantra novel, I was hooked. Now, the series is fifteen books in (with the sixteenth on the way), and about to release a prequel novel focused on one of my favorite characters (Severn). To say I am extremely excited would be an understatement.<br /><br />	As such, obviously I had to join the blog tour celebrating this new release. Part of that tour involves re-reading the series (yes!), and reviewing the novels we love so much. <br /><br />	Cast in Fury is the fourth novel in the Chronicles of Elantra series, and I would highly suggest reading them in order. The world and character building are so brilliant yet subtle, that you can really only see the larger picture if you see the story unfold in order.<br /><br />	Private Kaylin Neya has always had a talent for finding herself in situations over her head. Especially in a world that is as full of politics as it is a variety of species and races. Tensions and prejudice have been rising as of late, made worse by the events that played out in Cast in Secret.<br />	<br />While that nightmare is going on, Kaylin faces a much more personal dilemma, as her sergeant has been accused of murder. Worse, as it occurred within the caste, there's very little that Kaylin can do about it. At least, in the legal sense. Not that this has ever stopped Kaylin before. <br /><br />	“They feared you, and love can't exist when there's that much fear.”<br /><br />	Wow. I had forgotten how much I loved the earlier novels in this series. Well, if I'm being honest, I think I've absolutely adored each and every book, but it has been a hot minute since I did a full series re-read. <br /><br />	Cast in Fury is a compelling and emotional read – more so than the previous books, which is saying something. It provided some truly heartrending scenes, while also allowing for a deep dive into characters and races previously unexplored.<br /><br />	Marcus is one of those understated characters, easily leaned upon for a spot of humor during a moment of tension (though don't tell him that). Yet his life is so much more complex than it would appear at first glance – as evidenced by everything that occurred within this novel.<br /><br />	Once more, the already massive feeling world of Elantra seems to grow. It seems to happen every time we learn more about one of the races within the series. Since this isn't the first (or last) time that happens, it shows how large the world has and will become.<br />	<br />	“But she only knew one way of conquering fear, and that was to charge into it, blindly.”<br /><br />	What I especially love about the complexity of this world – and the characters – is that they all interact with one another. The politics in this world are unparalleled, bringing in a sense of realism to a world that could just as easily have been completely fantastical.<br /><br />	Combined with the magical systems, brilliant writing, and the world itself, this series will always find a way to capture my heart. Even as I read it again, for what must be nearing a dozen times. It's worth it every time.<br /><br />	Be sure to check out the two previous stops on this tour, as well as the rest of the following stops, right up until the release of The Emperor's Wolves! I know it's a novel that I am counting down the days for.<br /><br />Read more reviews over a <a href="https://quirkycatsfatstacks.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Quirky Cat's Fat Stacks</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9022131943457446399" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/747648-jeffrey?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/747648-jeffrey?shelf=read-in-2008">read-in-2008</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer28137177" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer577804726289393518">Kaylin Neya, a private in the investigative wing of the Empire's Hawks, bears on her body certain marks that have magical power. She is not the first to bear the marks. In prior books we have learned that she is able to use the marks to perform feats of magic and power that are the equal of the most powerful of the inhabitants of the land. The Emperor, who is a dragon lord, has assigned a Dragon Mage to teach Kaylin how to use the magic. Kaylin Neya has mostly used her power to help as a midwife</span>
  <span id="freeText577804726289393518" style="display:none">Kaylin Neya, a private in the investigative wing of the Empire's Hawks, bears on her body certain marks that have magical power. She is not the first to bear the marks. In prior books we have learned that she is able to use the marks to perform feats of magic and power that are the equal of the most powerful of the inhabitants of the land. The Emperor, who is a dragon lord, has assigned a Dragon Mage to teach Kaylin how to use the magic. Kaylin Neya has mostly used her power to help as a midwife for the various mothers of the races that make up the land, but she has been called upon to solve problems. In this novel, Kaylin must aid her sergeant, who is a Leontine, a race of giant catlike beings who has killed a friend, and his family and nephew, who is just a baby, but has a deadly heritage. She investigate the murder while also trying to protect the baby, and her investigation leads her to understand more about her unique abilities, why the baby's heritage may be his downfall and the death of all she holds dear. The action, while not as nonstop as in the past still shows that Kaylin Neya is a force to be reckoned with.<br /><br />A good read made better if you had read prior books </span>
  <a data-text-id="577804726289393518" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_33521885" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/33521885" />
    <a title="CJ - It&#39;s only a Paper Moon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1357098-cj---it-s-only-a-paper-moon"><img alt="CJ - It&#39;s only a Paper Moon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1437680885p2/1357098.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/33521885?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="CJ - It&#39;s only a Paper Moon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="CJ - It&#39;s only a Paper Moon" href="/user/show/1357098-cj---it-s-only-a-paper-moon">CJ - It&#39;s only a Paper Moon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of the series, character development in sci-fi/fantasy</span></div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer33521885" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11709342112798870637">My favorite of the series so far. Kaylin is growing up, slowly and painfully and well aware of her convictions. She is beginning to define herself by what she loves rather than what she is afraid of. She is slowly beginning to understand when silence is called for which was always Kaylin's problem.<br/><br/>The next book is entitled <i> Cast in Silence </i> I wonder if Kaylin is going to learn the value of silence even more :)<br/><br/>Severn is still a mystery but it is obvious that he cares for Kaylin because of who she</span>
  <span id="freeText11709342112798870637" style="display:none">My favorite of the series so far. Kaylin is growing up, slowly and painfully and well aware of her convictions. She is beginning to define herself by what she loves rather than what she is afraid of. She is slowly beginning to understand when silence is called for which was always Kaylin's problem.<br /><br />The next book is entitled <i> Cast in Silence </i> I wonder if Kaylin is going to learn the value of silence even more :)<br /><br />Severn is still a mystery but it is obvious that he cares for Kaylin because of who she is. Nightshade cares for Kaylin as well but I can't help but feel it's because of <i> what </i> she is.<br /><br />There were a few typos in this book and it was mostly names being actively used when the character had not shown up in a few hundred pages (Kaylin calling someone Marcus when Marcus was not in the scene nor had he been involved for a few hundred pages) or in another example when there is teasing going on between Marcus' wives and Kaylin is supposed to be speaking but the author put Kayala (another wife and definitely not the one speaking). It's nothing that a diligent copy editor/proof reader couldn't catch.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17348992947768708707">I am rereading the series with the audiobook and devouring them!<br/>This book goes into the legend/history of Leotines and we get to find out why the foundling hall was founded. We also get to see the family life Marcus leads and how Kaylin was adopted as part of the family. <br/><br/>The focus of the story is a question. Should we destroy something based on what one “might” become in the future or should we allow the chance for a better future? I love the way the story develops and explores the myths as well</span>
  <span id="freeText17348992947768708707" style="display:none">I am rereading the series with the audiobook and devouring them!<br />This book goes into the legend/history of Leotines and we get to find out why the foundling hall was founded. We also get to see the family life Marcus leads and how Kaylin was adopted as part of the family. <br /><br />The focus of the story is a question. Should we destroy something based on what one “might” become in the future or should we allow the chance for a better future? I love the way the story develops and explores the myths as well as the lives of Marcus’s wives. The connection between the dragons as the first born and the other creatures were fascinating, too.<br /><br />This series has become one of my favorite series and it is wonderful to listen! There is always something new to discover when you listen to it!<br /></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2906277-laura-kyahgirl?shelf=shapeshifters">shapeshifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2906277-laura-kyahgirl?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2906277-laura-kyahgirl?shelf=demons">demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2906277-laura-kyahgirl?shelf=gods-and-their-ilk">gods-and-their-ilk</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer449370494" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7357004057554359390">3.5/5; 4 stars; B+<br/><br/>Really enjoyed the insights in to the Leontine race, the Prideleas, etc in this book. The second half of the book was much stronger than the first half and I felt like the overall story was finally starting to gain momentum.<br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_558297406" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/558297406" />
    <a title="Kathy Davie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie"><img alt="Kathy Davie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285089902p2/4222001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/558297406?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathy Davie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy Davie" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie">Kathy Davie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer558297406" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16736335482395821666">Fourth in the Chronicles of Elantra fantasy series revolving around Kaylin Neya.<br/><br/><b>My Take</b><br/>Absolutely fascinating as Sagara expands on another of the civilizations that make up the inhabitants of Elantra, focusing on the Leontines this time, and we learn a great deal about its society, its culture and origins, and its stance on babies. Of Marrin's past and her reasons for starting the Foundling Halls. All of which Sagara uses to twist this tale of propaganda and murder. And, man, does she dribble ou</span>
  <span id="freeText16736335482395821666" style="display:none">Fourth in the Chronicles of Elantra fantasy series revolving around Kaylin Neya.<br /><br /><b>My Take</b><br />Absolutely fascinating as Sagara expands on another of the civilizations that make up the inhabitants of Elantra, focusing on the Leontines this time, and we learn a great deal about its society, its culture and origins, and its stance on babies. Of Marrin's past and her reasons for starting the Foundling Halls. All of which Sagara uses to twist this tale of propaganda and murder. And, man, does she dribble out the clues in tiny bits and pieces! Oh, wow, we also learn more of how the Outcaste Dragon became what he is.<br /><br />The central theme is fear. Fear of other cultures, fear of magic, fear of the government, fear of someone different from you, and the fear of how others will react to it. It's the fear of difference that is at the core of this particular story. Orogrim's difference causes hate, a hate that causes Orogrim's reactions now. The Tha'alani difference and their efforts to save Elantra raises fear and hate amongst the humans. What Kaylin brings, what we in the real world need to heed is tolerance, acceptance. Understanding. It's Kaylin's power of words that threaten Makuron. More terrifying to him than even the Dragonkiller.<br /><br />Giving and taking is a sub theme. The different permutations of give-and-take, taking, giving, and how Kaylin assesses the different peoples and cultures she knows.<br /><br />It's also a growth period for her as she learns patience and conformance. And if that isn't a curious evolution to watch! Poor Kaylin, LOL. And Mallory throws yet another demand upon her. It should be interesting to see if there's a follow-through. Kaylin does use her loyalty to Marcus and the Pridelea and her knowledge of the law to stay killing hands, and it's brilliant.<br /><br />Hmmm, Cultural Resource and Kaylin are not words that I would normally put together. It'll be interesting to see how Sagara fits them together. It's interesting to watch Kaylin/Rennick as she/he expounds on her/his particular prejudices only to find that they were pre-judging. There is an amazing ring of truth in each person's revelations that you can't help but appreciate for its subtlety. That whole confusion over lies and stories was excellent.<br /><br />Then there's the fascinating look inside a playwright's mind, how he thinks; his fascination with seemingly unrelated, unnecessary information, and how he chooses to convey an idea to an audience.<br /><br />I'm confused. If Kaylin was twenty-sixish in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9542.Cast_in_Shadow " target="_blank" title="Opens Michelle Sagara's Cast in Shadows in Goodreads" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Cast in Shadows</em>
</a>, 1, then how can she be thinking she might not see twenty-one in this story?<br /><br />I love watching as Rennick's perspective evolves from the "truth" of the gossip he's heard through to the truth of the Tha'alani people. It's a beautiful progression.<br /><br />We learn the power of words, of story.<br /><blockquote>"And in the end, it's Kaylin's words about trouble that are the most true:<br />'...if we <em>all</em> died at birth, nothing bad would ever happen.'"</blockquote><br /><br /><b>The Story</b><br />The people of Elantra are terrified and easily lash out at those they see as their enemy: the Tha'alani. Their actions at the waterfront in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/641910.Cast_In_Secret" title="Opens Michelle Sagara's Cast in Secret in Goodreads" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Cast in Secret</em>
</a>, 3, have cast them as mankind's enemies, eager for human deaths. It's an easy role for the humans to push the Tha'alani into as Kaylin knows. Not so long ago, she saw them as evil as well.<br /><br />Now it's up to Kaylin and Severn to teach Rennick how to truly see.<br /><br />Because that's not enough of a challenge, Marcus has been arrested for murder.<br /><br /><b>The Characters</b><br /><strong>Private Lord Kaylin Neya</strong> of the Hawks is a special case and not just in the Hawks. It's the tattoos in the Old Tongue that have made her more than a curiosity, and for such a lowly person, she has friends in some very high places.<br /><br /><strong>Corporal Lord Severn Handred</strong> grew up with Kaylin. And earned his lordly title in the same time and place she did in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30189.Cast_In_Courtlight" title="Opens Michelle Sagara's Cast in Courtlight in Goodreads" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Cast in Courtlight</em>
</a>, 2. Estranged for years, Kaylin has finally learned the truth of his actions, and they are partners in the Hawks. <br /><br /><strong>Lord Sanabalis</strong> is one of four Dragon lords at the Imperial Court and the mage who will continue to work with Kaylin to understand her powers. <strong>Lord Tiamaris</strong>, a Dragon, worked with Kaylin and Severn in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9542.Cast_in_Shadow " target="_blank" title="Opens Michelle Sagara's Cast in Shadows in Goodreads" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Cast in Shadows</em>
</a>, 1 and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/641910.Cast_In_Secret" title="Opens Michelle Sagara's Cast in Secret in Goodreads" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Cast in Secret</em>
</a>, and now he will assist them in their hunt for Orogrim and the black dragon. The <strong>Arkon</strong> is the Dragon whose hoard is the Imperial Libraries and the galleries.<br /><br /><strong>Richard Rennick</strong> is the Imperial Playwright charged with interpreting events in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/641910.Cast_In_Secret" title="Opens Michelle Sagara's Cast in Secret in Goodreads" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Cast in Secret</em>
</a> to redirect the peoples' anger. And he's clueless. <br /><br /><blockquote>And, as Marcus points out:<br />"You took a man that makes <em>you</em> look tactful to the Tha'alani Quarter."</blockquote><br /><br /><strong>Marrin</strong> is the Leontine who organized the Foundling Halls for the human orphans; cross her at your peril. <strong>Amos</strong> is the Hall's guard and gardener. <strong>Dock</strong> and <strong>Cassie</strong> are two of the foundlings.<br /><br /><strong>Evanton</strong>, the Keeper of an elemental garden, has been dragged in to help with makeup. <br /><br /><em>The Hawks include:</em><br />Well, not Ironjaw, more formally known as Sergeant <strong>Marcus</strong> Kassan, is in jail, and one of Kaylin's worst enemies---<strong>Constant Mallory</strong> from Missing Persons---is in his place, handing out the assignments, looking to destroy Kaylin, and making everyone in and out of the office absolutely miserable. <strong>Perenne</strong>, <strong>Tanner</strong>, <strong>Breen</strong>, and <strong>Clint</strong> (of the enticing flight feathers!) are Aerians and worried about Kaylin keeping her job. The <strong>Quartermaster</strong> usually hates Kaylin---she keeps bringing back damaged equipment. Now he's conspiring. <strong>Moran</strong> is Aerian and the Hawks' medic.<br /><br /><em>The Leontines</em><br /><strong>Kayala</strong> is the <em>Mrryn</em>, Matriarch, of the Pridelea, Marcus' wives, along with <strong>Tessa</strong>, <strong>Graylin</strong>, <strong>Reesa</strong>, and <strong>Sarabe</strong>. And we learn more about Leontine culture and the importance of fur color. The <strong>Elders</strong> rule the Leontine neighborhood. One of them was <strong>Gorran</strong>, a friend of Marcus'. <strong>Adar of the Claw</strong> is the Leontine castelord, and First Son; they call Sanabalis, Eldest. <br /><br /><strong>Arlan/Marai</strong> is a Leontine, Sarabe's sister, whom Kaylin helped in the birthing of her son, <strong>Roshan Kaylarr</strong>. The same one she was invited to lick in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/641910.Cast_In_Secret" title="Opens Michelle Sagara's Cast in Secret in Goodreads" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Cast in Secret</em>
</a>, with all that this implies in Leontine culture. It enables Kaylin to claim Pridelea, even though Arlan is not in one. <strong>Orogrim</strong> is Outcaste, a Leontine mage, with deadly plans for Roshan. <br /><br /><em>The Tha'alani</em><br />Used to delve inside a person's mind, their touch is not usually delicate. For this and the rape of one's mind, the <strong>Tha'alani</strong>, a.k.a., Truthseekers, are feared, hated. What the public doesn't know is that this is the compromise the Tha'alani were forced to make, to serve the Emperor or become piles of ash. <strong>Ybelline Rabon'alani</strong> is the Emperor's Tha'alani and the castelord of her people. <strong>Sergeant Voone</strong> of the Swords is helping to protect them. <strong>Ellis</strong> is the very young heir to the castelord.<br /><br /><strong>Lord Nightshade</strong>, an outcaste Barrani fieflord, provides new information about the fiefs, and holds Dragonkiller, <em>Meliannos</em>. <em>From what I can gather, he's indicated that Kaylin will be his </em>Erenne<em>, and the best I can figure is that he intends her to be his consort or wife??</em> <strong>Lord Andellen</strong>, one of the Barrani guards with Kaylin in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30189.Cast_In_Courtlight" title="Opens Michelle Sagara's Cast in Courtlight in Goodreads" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Cast in Courtlight</em>
</a>, is fighting alongside them both.<br /><br />The Outcaste Dragon Lord, <strong>Makuron the Black</strong>, is still alive and plotting.<br /><br /><em>The peacekeeping forces of Elantra</em><br />There are three peacekeeping forces and three Lords of Law: the Lord of Hawks, <strong>Lord Grammayre</strong>, the Hawklord, heads up the Hawks---the investigators; the <strong>Lord of Swords</strong> and his men are the peacekeepers---the street cops, if you will; and, <strong>Lord Merlin</strong>, the Lord of Wolves and his people are its black ops with the Shadow Wolves the "darkest face the Law could turn on the populace". <br /><br />Think of the <strong>Aerians</strong> as birdmen, but not shifters. <strong>Barrani</strong> are the upper class in this society, although not the uppermost. Vicious, cruel, and they seem to have the appearance of what I would consider Fey. The <strong>Leontine</strong> are lion shifters. <strong>Arcanists</strong> are mages who work independently of the Dragon Emperor. <br /><br /><strong>Fieflords</strong> are independent conquerors of the seven large criminal neighborhoods outside the city proper. The <strong>fiefs</strong> themselves have always existed, a metaphysical "solidity that defies the darkness, erodes it" where the "land and the Lord are almost one", an ancient binding, twisted. The heart of the fiefs is <strong>
  <em>Ravellon</em>
</strong>, a fief none dare enter. <em>I think it makes Nightshade look benign!</em><br /><br /><b>The Cover</b><br />The cover is shades of pink and lavender as the even-more tattooed Kaylin, in a very sexy lavender slip dress, appears to hold back a tidal wave.<br /><br />The title is the response of the people of Elantra, <em>Cast in Fury</em> in their perception of the Tha'alani actions that day in the previous story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16736335482395821666" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3419837467" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3419837467" />
    <a title="Toubob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/74049198-toubob"><img alt="Toubob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591938958p2/74049198.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3419837467?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Toubob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Toubob" href="/user/show/74049198-toubob">Toubob</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/30360944-cast-in-fury">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3419837467" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18042436546224886649">I listened to this book through audibles romance program. This is NOT a romance. The author set it up to have a possible romance between 2 different men and then has completely ignored the situation. Only a few books even mention the situation with a couple of sentences (I have read through book 9). <br/><br/>The books have become very predictable <br/>1. MC complains about lack of sleep/food/time/respect etc<br/>2. MC is blamed for things that were caused by other people/situations<br/>3. MC complains/fumbles anything </span>
  <span id="freeText18042436546224886649" style="display:none">I listened to this book through audibles romance program. This is NOT a romance. The author set it up to have a possible romance between 2 different men and then has completely ignored the situation. Only a few books even mention the situation with a couple of sentences (I have read through book 9). <br /><br />The books have become very predictable <br />1. MC complains about lack of sleep/food/time/respect etc<br />2. MC is blamed for things that were caused by other people/situations<br />3. MC complains/fumbles anything to do with her magic<br />4. MC is tasked with saving person/group/world<br />5. MC saves person/group/world with words though never knows how she did it<br />6. MC is never thanked/paid/acknowledged for the save<br />7. MC is punishes/derogated/disciplined/threatened for small things that happened with the save<br /><br />The author goes on and on and on and on about the MC working with words to the point that I think it puts me in a hypnotic mind frame. Eventually the tension is resolved. I have no idea how. But it takes a lot of talking about it. <br /><br />I think this is the only book series that I don’t like because of the lack of character development. I normally rail about character driven books. I prefer plot driven books. This series needs to have some character development. The author should not have brought up issues/situations between different characters to only ignore the dynamics between the characters. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18042436546224886649" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YRrOhzegLLZoogcNnIuiv2nNtyfaXdbGbCx6uJ12aD9rA6PTyW/VB+ko6moVqpOaNXPZgHGMHXCj2aBlJDrovg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('JsmLb8z00Gg1LHzp7IpkdSGgbCPLTMgGaAE1M13JV3ss0OY7Mjsp2bSmkY5lq1VQfR4ChGCdA7Cn9O/u5IXX+g==')})
  }
